Private Postal Bureau Caught Smuggling 139

Causing Delays

On the 7th of this month, around 5:00 PM, Shanghai Postal Administration inspectors discovered 29 smuggled postal parcels of various sizes belonging to private postal bureaus on the Xinning Shaoxing steamer. The parcels contained over a thousand letters. The inspectors investigated on board, but no one claimed responsibility. Later, in cooperation with the waterway police, the parcels were taken to the waterway patrol headquarters, where the chief officer confirmed the findings. Knowing they could not deny the smuggling, the private postal bureau representatives went to the post office to claim the items. The post office will follow regulations, requiring them to pay fines and make up postage before retrieving and re-mailing the letters. However, the letters have already been significantly delayed.

Rescuing Sand Boats Hijacked Near Songkou 140

Due to poor fishing conditions this year, the Shandong sand boats Gao Changmao, Ding Dexing, Ye Tongsheng, Jin Wanshun, and Jin Zengxiang had to return to Shandong early. Some planned to load dried fish at Beikou in early May. While sailing from Songkou, they were suddenly hijacked by a large group of pirates in the waters of Sanjia and Wai Yu Shan Hongyang. The pirates demanded a large ransom for the boats, as previously reported. After two months with no news, it has recently been reported that Captain Ye of the Sixth Zhejiang Offshore Water Police Team led his officers into a fierce battle with the pirates on the 6th of this month. As a result, all of the boats belonging to Gao Changmao and others were rescued. Upon hearing the news, the boat owners were overjoyed and plan to gather in Taiwan to take possession of their vessels.

Madwoman's Incoherent Ramblings 141

Claims to Have Killed Two Black Fish with a Knife

Unaware of Killing Two People

Jiang Xu, a woman from Wuxi with a history of mental illness, was admitted to the Xinpu Yutang Hospital for treatment of another illness last month. Unfortunately, her old illness relapsed, and she killed two female patients in the hospital with a knife. The hospital reported this to the local court, and the prosecutor filed a public prosecution for murder. Yesterday, Judge Zhao held a court hearing. The woman claimed that after recovering from her illness, she saw two black fish and killed them with a knife to cook and eat them quickly. She claimed she was unaware of killing two people and that she was possessed by vengeful spirits, not responsible for her actions. The judge deemed her statements incoherent and ordered her to be sent back to the hospital for further treatment and sentencing after clarification.

Zhu Jixing Case Scheduled for Sentencing 142

Final Arguments Made Yesterday

Zhu Jixing, a deputy comprador at Wing On Bank, embezzled over ten thousand taels of bank funds and fled. After the bank accused the accountants Xie Tonghou and Yu Xiling, Zhu was apprehended. The case has been repeatedly covered in the newspapers. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Jiashi held a hearing, bringing the three defendants to court for final arguments. First, the police lawyer Gan Jingxian argued that defendant Zhu Jixing embezzled over 160,000 taels by replacing customer's bank drafts with bad checks, accumulating a large amount over time that he could not cover. When he fled, he instructed Zheng Hekang, a partner in his Dexing Sugar Company, to deposit a forged Yifeng bank draft at the Si Ming Bank. The Si Ming Bank discovered the forgery and detained Zheng. Seeing his plan fail, Zhu had no choice but to flee. He has now fully admitted to the charges and should be punished according to the law. Although Yu Xiling is suspected of collusion, his involvement is minor compared to Xie Tonghou.

Next, the defendants' lawyers Jiang Yi, Ping and Jiang Baoli defended, stating that Zhu Jixing acknowledged his despicable actions of forging bank drafts and embezzling large sums. However, his actions were driven by circumstances. Zhu had previously guaranteed debts for others, incurring significant losses. He sought to recover his wealth through speculation but was unsuccessful. His sugar company also suffered significant losses due to the gold-silver ratio. Overwhelmed by these problems, Zhu saw no other option than to flee, seeking a way to rectify the situation. The fact that he did not take any money with him suggests that he did not intend to embezzle. The lawyers requested leniency from the court and a suspended sentence if punishment was necessary. They argued that Yu Xiling was found innocent of any suspicion during the police investigation and requested his release. As for Xie Tonghou, he was acting under Zhu's orders, and any mistakes were Zhu's responsibility. The lawyers requested the court to consider these points.

After the lawyers finished their arguments, Judge Xu announced that sentencing would be on July 19th. Zhu Jixing was taken back into custody by the police, while Yu and Xie were allowed to be released on bail.

Rickshaw Puller

Suspected of Conspiring in a Robbery 144

Suzhou Woman Robbed Upon Arrival in Shanghai

The night train from Nanjing to Shanghai arrived at the North Railway Station around 1:00 AM yesterday. A middle-aged woman, Shen Wu, a native of Suzhou, arrived in Shanghai with her fourteen-year-old son, Shen Jiacheng. They hired two rickshaws to take them to the Zhenhua Hotel at the intersection of Fuzhou Road and Guangxi Road. However, as they passed the eastern section of Ke Neng Hai Road and Qipu Road, they were stopped by several robbers. One robber brandished a pistol and threatened Shen, stealing a suitcase containing silver dollars, clothing, and bank books worth over one hundred yuan. Shen shouted for help, and the local police station was nearby. Upon hearing the call, Hua Detective Wang Jie and Western Detective No. 263 arrived, but the robbers had already escaped with the loot.

After questioning Shen, the police suspected the two rickshaw pullers, Yang Asi from Chongming and Zhu Qingbang from Haimen, of conspiring with the robbers. The police reasoned that from the railway station to the Zhenhua Hotel, they should have taken the concession road to North Zhejiang Road, crossed the Old Garbage Bridge to Zhejiang Road, and then turned into Fuzhou Road. Instead, the two rickshaw pullers took Ke Neng Hai Road to the Qipu Road intersection, turning east instead of west, which was suspicious. The police took both rickshaw pullers to the police station, reported the situation to the chief, and were instructed to detain them and send them to the Shanghai Special District Court for questioning.

Xu Zhou Sold to the Northeast 145

A Heartbreaking Story of a Weak Woman

Xu Hongzhen, a 28-year-old Tianjin native, worked as a policeman in the Shihui Port Water Patrol Team. His wife, Zhou, a 22-year-old native of Songjiang, met Li Jinfeng, a woman from Anhui, on July 14th of last year. Li invited Zhou to visit the Changsha steamer at the Huangpu Wharf. The ship suddenly set sail, and Zhou was unable to disembark. She had no choice but to follow Li Jinfeng to Qingdao, effectively being driven by Li. After spending a night in Qingdao, she met Li Jinfeng's lover, Tong Shaoying. However, the plan was discovered by the local Public Security Bureau, and all three men and women were detained. Tong Shaoying managed to prove via telegram that the two women were his wives, and they were released.

In mid-September, Tong took Xu Zhou to Dalian, where they met an (old man) who inquired about Zhou's desire to return to Shanghai. Zhou said she wanted to go, so she followed him. However, she was tricked into going to Changchun and sold to the Feihong brothel for 800 yuan. At this point, Xu Zhou was trapped and helpless. She managed to send a letter to her husband, Xu Hongzhen, in Shanghai, asking for help. Xu reported this to the Women and Children's Relief Association, which informed the Fengtian Association to contact the Jilin Public Security Bureau. Zhou was rescued and set off for Shanghai on May 12th, arriving on June 28th.

The other day, a friend of Xu Hongzhen saw Li Jinfeng, who had lured Zhou out of the country, at the North Station Hotel on the Concession Road. He informed Zhou, who took Li to the Fifth District Public Security Bureau in Zhabei for investigation. Li Jinfeng confessed that Tong Shaoying had sold Xu Zhou and that she was unaware of it. Li also said that she was bought by Tong into the Jinhong brothel in Siping Street, Changchun, for 200 yuan. A customer helped her redeem herself a month ago, and she came to Shanghai. The district chief ruled to send the case to the Judicial Section for review.

Accusation of Missing Female Worker 146

Zhang Zhengang, residing at No. 8 Dingsheng Lane, Avenue Joffre, French Concession, brought a woman named Zhang Erbao to the Second District Police Station, accusing her of causing his daughter to run away. He claimed that his daughter, Zhang Yunbao, 17 years old, worked at the Yunjian Sock Factory on Jiangyin Street, Xiaoximen, since January of this year. She was initially well-behaved, but after becoming sworn sisters with Zhang Erbao, another female worker at the factory, Zhang Yunbao's attitude changed drastically. Zhang Erbao often took Zhang Yunbao to the Great World amusement park. As a result, Zhang Yunbao became frivolous. Zhang Zhengang forbade his daughter from working at the sock factory to prevent her corruption. However, on the night of the 7th of this month, Zhang Yunbao ran away, taking 104 yuan in cash and clothing with her. Zhang Zhengang believed that Zhang Erbao was heavily implicated in the disappearance and requested an investigation.

Zhang Erbao, 22 years old, residing at Jinjiazhai Jin'an Lane, Chezhan Road, testified that she used to work at the Yunjian Sock Factory. Zhang Yunbao started learning at the factory in January of this year. She helped Zhang Yunbao learn the ropes as Zhang Yunbao was kind and well-behaved, so Zhang Yunbao had a good relationship with her. But Zhang Erbao had been bedridden since March of this year due to illness and had not fully recovered, so she had not been to the sock factory in three months. She also claimed that she had not been to the Great World or New World amusement parks with Zhang Yunbao and had rarely left her house. She claimed that she was wrongly accused of enticing Zhang Yunbao to run away.

The police station, finding conflicting statements, transferred the case to the District Court for trial.

Page 16

A Dumpling in a Divorce Case 148

Is it Poisoned? A Matter Worth Investigating

Qin Guangfu, a native of Qingjiang, has hired Lawyer Liu Xiang to sue his wife, Qin Sun, at the District Court for abuse and attempted harm, seeking a divorce to prevent future troubles. His statement alleges that he married the defendant, Sun, in his hometown during the Xuantong reign. After living in the village for several years, his wife complained about his lack of success, leading to frequent arguments. Later, a fellow villager helped him find a job driving, so he and his wife came to Shanghai. They initially lived near the Shanghai Military Camp. The plaintiff left early and returned late, while the defendant gambled every day. Upon learning this, the plaintiff advised her to stop, but she refused. The defendant was even more unruly than before. In December of last year, the defendant would frequently go out on various pretexts. The plaintiff tried to advise her, but the defendant accused him of having an affair. When the plaintiff returned home from work at night, the defendant would suspect him and force him to drink a large bowl of cold water before he could sleep. If he did not comply, she would verbally abuse him. This abuse was not unusual. Since this month, she has been taking his clothes and hiding them elsewhere. Arguments have been frequent. On the 24th of last month, the defendant wanted to eat noodles and dumplings. When the plaintiff returned home in the afternoon, the defendant said that she had saved dumplings to cook. The defendant cooked the dumplings and took them out. The plaintiff noticed that the soup tasted strange and was black. Upon closer inspection, several of the dumplings had a bluish-black color. The plaintiff was afraid to try them, but the defendant said loudly that they were not poisoned and that she would eat them first. The defendant then secretly opened the back door and poured the dumplings into the drain, intending to destroy the evidence. At this point, the plaintiff realized something was amiss. He rushed to grab one dumpling. The neighbors knew about this. The defendant usually neglected household affairs. After the plaintiff noticed the dumplings were strange, she tried to destroy them, which raised suspicions. Therefore, he requests a divorce.

Yesterday morning, Judge Zhao specially opened the First Court for trial. The plaintiff, Qin Guangfu, testified to the previous events and presented the dumpling as evidence for inspection. The defendant, Qin Sun, testified that she and her husband had always been on good terms and had no malicious intentions. She claimed that her husband wanted to divorce her because he had a new lover, who was also married, and that she did not want a divorce. The judge stated that the dumpling incident was important and needed to be investigated thoroughly. The judge ordered that the hearing would not be opened for debate today and that the witnesses who saw the event at the time should be summoned to court for further trial.

French Businessman Sapo

Sues Yunfei Automobile Driver 149

Seeking Full Compensation for the Car Price

Mrs. Mije Demands Compensation for Losses

French businessman Sapo, represented by lawyer Ba He, filed a lawsuit with the French Court stating that the plaintiff's car number 630 was driven to the intersection of Fulili Road and Qiqi Road on the evening of the 9th of last month when it was hit by car number 12331, driven by Shen Yunfei of Yunfei Automobile Company at 77 Huanlong Road. The defendant ignored the red light signal and completely wrecked the plaintiff's car number 630. Mrs. Mije and her son were seriously injured. The defendant deliberately violated traffic regulations. The plaintiff requested that the court be ruled on in accordance with the regulations and also sought compensation for the car price of 2,850 taels.

Furthermore, Mrs. Mije's representative, lawyer Mu Di Yi, stated that his client and her son were sitting in car number 630 when the defendant's driver's negligence caused the car to be wrecked, resulting in Mrs. Mije's serious injury. She is still in the hospital and has not yet recovered. According to the Western doctor's examination, Mrs. Mije suffered severe internal injuries that will be difficult to recover from. Since Mrs. Mije runs a Western-style clothing store and earns 2,000 yuan per month, she had to hire a replacement, paying a monthly salary of 500 yuan. The loss should be compensated for at least 10,000 taels. The son was also injured in the brain, which should be compensated for 500 taels.

Western Detective Captain Sa Cai Er testified that the accident was caused by the defendant's driver violating the regulations. Police regulations require cars to slow down when driving through the area and pay attention to whether the standing officer is signaling a red light. Detectives No. 21 (Chinese) and No. 407 (Vietnamese) testified that the red light was on that evening, and the defendant should have stopped. However, the defendant ignored the signal, causing the accident, which is undeniable. The court was asked to investigate.

The defendant, represented by lawyer Ti Baike, argued that the case was a traffic violation, and the plaintiff's request for an incidental civil suit was inappropriate. The lawyer declined to comment on the cause of the accident, saying that it was difficult to prove who was at fault. The defendant's car saw a green light from the officer when it arrived at the intersection, so the defendant proceeded. The police officers had the responsibility to prove the defendant's fault. The lawyer asked the court to dismiss the case. After a lengthy exchange between the lawyers, the Chinese and Western judges announced that the arguments were over and that they would decide on the case.

New Building for the Young Women's Christian Association (YWCA) 159

The Young Women's Christian Association (YWCA) at No. 19 Yuanmingyuan Road is currently in a building that was constructed 70 years ago. Due to the daily expansion of the association's business and the expansion of operations, it is now considered cramped and insufficient for its needs, and the building is old and potentially dangerous. Therefore, this spring, the committee of the association decided to rebuild a magnificent new association building within two years to reorganize its affairs. The old site and the buildings at Nos. 18 and 20 were demolished and leveled in May, hoping to start construction on a seven-story office building in the shortest possible time. To save construction costs and land, they also plan to build several low houses on the roof for hosting guests and lodging travelers, as in the old Dongdao Lu. In the future, the various offices of the association will be located on the seventh floor, with the other six floors available for rent. The land was originally the remaining land of the British Consulate and was acquired by the United States YWCA in 1921. In 1927, the association formally donated the land to the Chinese YWCA in its entirety as a permanent foundation. As for the construction costs of the new building, half of the funds are gifts from Mr. Karen, Ms. Toler, and several other Westerners. Barring unforeseen obstacles, the groundbreaking ceremony for the new building will be held in August or September. The new building will be the largest women's organization office building in Shanghai.

Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities Penalties

Unjustified Increase in Ferry Fare at Tanzhi Bay West Ferry 160

After the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities reorganized the Wusong River ferry crossings, the ferries presented a completely new look. The ferry fare for each passenger was originally one copper coin. However, the ferry operators claimed that the cost of living continued to rise, and their income was insufficient to cover their expenses. Therefore, in April of this year, they repeatedly submitted requests to the Bureau of Public Utilities, asking for permission to increase the fare to two copper coins per passenger. The Bureau sent personnel to investigate the actual income and expenses of each ferry and then forwarded the matter to the Municipal Government for approval. However, the Tanzhi Bay West Ferry had a considerable surplus with a fare of one copper coin per passenger, and was ordered to continue charging the same fare. Subsequently, the ferry operator, Gong A'nan, disregarding the situation, followed the crowd and changed the fare to two copper coins per passenger. The Bureau of Public Utilities, after learning of this, considered the unauthorized increase in fare without prior approval to be inappropriate and reported it to the Municipal Government for a fine of one hundred yuan to be used for repairing the ferry pier. Later, the ferry operator formally submitted a request for a fare increase, but the Municipal Government, considering the livelihood of ordinary people, did not approve it.

Continuation of Hongkou Epidemic Hospital This Year 161

The Hongkou Epidemic Hospital in this city was initiated and funded by enthusiastic public figures such as Zhu Jing'an, Chen Silan, and Xi Derun in the sixteenth year of the Republic of China. Zhu and the other two were appointed as directors, with Lin Chunshan and Zhu Xiaofang as directors of medical affairs, and Dong Gengsan and Tang Jingshou as directors of administrative affairs. Their achievements were remarkable. In the seventeenth year, the hospital continued to expand, and there were plans to purchase land and build a permanent structure. When the Shanghai Municipal Government was established, Director Zhu and others handed over the hospital to the Health Bureau. Unfortunately, the Municipal budget had already been finalized, and there was no way to cover the expenses, leading to a de facto shutdown in the eighteenth year. Now, local figures, noting the increasing prosperity and population of the area around Hujiamuqiao in Hongkou, as well as the growing number of factories, and the inevitability of epidemics, have requested Zhu and others to continue operating the hospital, relying on their experience. It is reported that Zhu and others have agreed. On the evening of the tenth of this month, they gathered local figures at the Atlantic Restaurant to discuss the continuation procedures, which will soon be implemented. However, it is reported that Xi Derun has firmly declined the position of director due to personal reasons, and Shen Huachen has been appointed to succeed him. Furthermore, economic director Wang Shenfu, due to being overburdened, has been replaced by Zhang Peilian, who has been jointly appointed by Director Zhu and others.

Record of the Fourth Annual Meeting of the Leprosy Association 166

Election of Directors for This Term

Since its establishment, the China Leprosy Relief Association has devoted itself to planning and relief efforts for leprosy for over four years, sparing no effort. Its enthusiasm and perseverance have long been praised by people from all walks of life. Yesterday (the 12th) at 4:30 p.m., the association held its fourth annual meeting at the YMCA on Sichuan Road. Directors and members such as Diao Xinde, Kuang Fuzhuo, Shen Gao (representative of the Health Bureau), Chen Lengseng (representative of the Social Affairs Bureau), Mrs. Xiao Zhiji, Zhu Shaoping, Cheng Lian, and Li Yuanxin, as well as people from all walks of life, attended. The meeting was presided over by Chairman Li Yuanxin. A detailed report was made, describing the various works of the association. Some notable achievements include publishing the Leprosy Quarterly, sending representatives to various ports to investigate the leprosy situation, and subsidizing the expenses of leprosy hospitals in various places. Last year alone, donations for the treatment of leprosy with the most effective chaulmoogra oil exceeded thousands of gold coins. In addition, the association took over the Hongkou Commune in this city, providing diagnosis and treatment. The final conclusion stated that the Shanghai Leprosy Hospital has been in preparation for a long time, but there is no suitable site for construction. The only hope for the future is to overcome all difficulties and see its early completion. Subsequently, Treasurer Cheng Lian reported on the annual income and expenditure accounts. Then, Dr. Wu Liande, Director of the National Seaport Quarantine Service, gave a speech, followed by Dr. Mai Yagu, Far East Representative of the International Leprosy Relief Association, who spoke on "Methods for Eradicating Leprosy in China." His words were pertinent and incisive. Lastly, Mr. Yu Zhijian gave a speech on "The Five-Year Movement for Leprosy Relief," outlining a grand and ambitious plan as follows: 1. Conduct a thorough leprosy survey; 2. Compile leprosy facts into teaching materials for schools; 3. Participate in urban sanitation campaigns in various places; 4. Organize a Central Leprosy Association; 5. Convene a national leprosy conference; 6. Urge the government to promulgate leprosy laws; 7. Build at least one leprosy hospital in each affected province; 8. Establish at least one leprosy clinic in each major city; 9. Hold a national student leprosy eradication speech contest every year; 10. Find ways to protect and nurture the children of leprosy patients; 11. Find employment for cured leprosy patients. If the above plans can be realized, it is certain that the scourge of leprosy will be eradicated forever. It is hoped that people from all walks of life will provide deep assistance to promote its early realization. By the time the meeting adjourned, thousands of homes were lit up. On the same day, the association elected the following directors: Li Yuanxin, Kuang Fuzhuo, Li Guansen, Cheng Lian, Li Denghui, Yan Fuqing, Diao Xinde, Han Yulin, Gu Enkang, Wu Jingyao, Mrs. Xiao Zhiji, Mrs. Zheng Yangxiu, Wang Zhiren, Zhu Shaoping, Li Qifan; honorary directors: Liu Hongsheng, Sa Kesun.

Wu Song Ship Donation Office

Reward for Finding Lost Stamps 168

When collecting ship donations, the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Finance's urban area ship donation office prints a kind of stamp ticket to be pasted on the donation ticket as proof. This kind of stamp ticket is divided into several grades according to the size of the sailboat. At about 12 o'clock in the morning of the previous day, Sha Liuting, a tax collector from the Wusong ship donation branch, collected ship donations outside and returned to the office at the intersection of Waitan and Dongsheng Road. Sha felt an urgent need and placed the tax collection bag on the writing desk. After Sha returned from the toilet, he immediately went back to his lodging for lunch. Unexpectedly, when Sha went out to collect taxes again at 1 p.m., he inspected the bag and found that 47 sixth-grade ship donation stamps placed in the bag had suddenly disappeared. Sha, the tax collector, considered that the 40 stamps were worth a total of 517 yuan, which was a major concern. He was extremely shocked and immediately reported the incident to the branch director, Zhuo Xianggeng. After receiving the report, Director Zhuo believed that if these stamps were stolen and used by bandits, it would greatly affect the collection of ship donations. He immediately investigated the office staff and public servants in detail, but because he did not know when Sha, the tax collector, lost the stamps, it became a suspicious case. Director Zhuo immediately sent a letter to the Seventh District Public Security Bureau to request an arrest, and printed hundreds of advertisements, posted them everywhere, and offered a reward of six yuan to find the lost stamps. It was not until about 1 p.m. yesterday that a patrolman from the Seventh District, accompanied by an old woman surnamed Bai, sent the above-mentioned stamp tickets to the ship donation office, claiming that they were picked up on the road. This was obviously a cover-up. Director Zhuo, since the stamps had been returned, did not want to investigate further, and gave her the reward money and sent her away.

Robbery and Assault in Yangjing Town 172

Thief Qin Yenao Apprehended

At the home of Han Daxian in Hanjiazhai, south of Yangjing Town, Pudong, six or seven local thieves with weapons broke into the house at 11 p.m. last night, while others kept watch outside. Han was not yet asleep. The thieves entered the room and pinned Han to the ground, covering his mouth and questioning him about where he had hidden the raffle winnings and gold jewelry he had obtained during the day. At that time, Tang Jinghuan, director of the Second Branch of the Third District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and Inspector Wang Deshan were patrolling with police officers due to the unstable situation. They heard the sound and rushed to apprehend the thieves, capturing one local thief, Qin Yenao, on the spot. They took him to the station for questioning. Qin's confession was cunning and he denied any robbery. The station ordered the victim, Han Daxian, to be carried to the station after dawn for identification. He identified Qin as one of the thieves who entered his house last night. Qin then confessed that he was involved in the robbery of Han's house. Director Tang obtained the confession and immediately prepared a document to escort the thief Qin to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Cohabitation Based on Agreement 175

Freedom if They Don't Agree

Ding Lingzhen, a local woman, is 23 years old. Her father died early, and she struggled with her mother. At the age of 16, she worked at the Dacheng Factory in Yangshupu and was seduced by the foreman's concubine, who claimed that a worker in the same factory, Zhang Maoao, also a local, had not yet married. The woman was deceived and rented a house with Zhang Maoao in Zhoujiazai and cohabited there for eight years. At first, Zhang provided some financial assistance, but later, the woman relied entirely on her wages to support the family. In October of last year, the woman fell ill and was bedridden. Zhang Maoao disappeared. The woman suffered from poverty and illness, and her rent was in arrears for several months. She was evicted by the landlord and forced to leave the house. The woman then resided at the home of her sister, Wu Ding, and notified Zhang Maoao. Unexpectedly, Zhang ignored her. The woman believed that Zhang should not abandon her after their relationship began, and she regretted her past. She sought help and wanted to separate from him to avoid suffering. Therefore, she hired lawyer Wang Chengkuan to file a lawsuit in the Local Court against Zhang Maoao for abandonment, requesting a judgment to dissolve their relationship. Yesterday morning, presiding judge Zhao Zhenhai opened the second court for trial. The defendant did not appear in court because his address was unknown and he could not be served. The plaintiff, Ding Lingzhen, testified about the past and requested permission to separate. Judge Zhao obtained the testimony and asked, "Are you officially married or just cohabitating?" She replied, "We are just cohabitating." Judge Zhao said, "Since you are just cohabitating, there is no need to request a separation. If a father and son separate, it is to sever the father-son relationship. If it is a husband and wife, it is to sever the family relationship. You are just cohabitating, there is no need to request it. If you agree, you cohabitate; if you don't agree, you are free to do as you please. There is no such provision in the law." The woman claimed that she was afraid of future troubles, so she came to request it. Judge Zhao understood her situation and said, "You should withdraw this case. It should be recorded in the minutes that if the defendant has any illegal actions, there will be legal sanctions. There is no need to worry too much." The woman listened and immediately requested to withdraw the case, signed, and left the court.

Free Talk

Let it go with a laugh, Overseas Guest 183

Young man to old man: I really love your daughter. For her, I can go through fire and water. Even if I die immediately, I would be a thousand two hundred times willing.

Old man: You're lying. I don't believe you.

Young man: I'm completely sincere. How can you say I'm lying?

Old man: Because I said the same thing when I proposed to my old wife. That's why I know you're lying.

Petitioner: Sir, I've said so much just now. I'm really sorry for disturbing your peace.

Great Gentleman: Fortunately, I was just thinking about other things here. I didn't hear a word of what you said just now.

Doctor: Your illness hasn't improved yet. I only need to come five or six more times and it will take effect. Here's the bill for the medical expenses. Please take a look.

Patient: Please don't show it to me right now. If I see it, I'm afraid my illness will get worse. Please also skip the next five or six times. Because every time you come, it will make my illness worse by one point.

A: You told Mr. D that you have an income of 9,999 yuan per year. Why didn't you honestly say 10,000 yuan? What's the big deal about that one yuan difference?

B: If I blurted out 10,000 yuan, he would think it was a very large amount when he heard the word "ten thousand" and would inevitably be shocked. It's better to say less to avoid alarming people.

Smell and Love by Ms. Yeh Hua 184

Smell is olfaction, also written as stench. It is a terrestrial sense, akin to the eleventh sense. It's one of the external senses, evolved from the sensitivity of single-celled organisms. The olfactory organ is simple, its nerves located on the upper part of the nasal bridge, directly reaching the brown mucous membrane. It receives chemical gaseous stimuli. There are only six types of smells: medicinal, floral, fruity, fatty, putrid, and fishy; all others are mixtures. Odors like body odor are a mixture of burnt and putrid; rancid smells are a mixture of putrid and fatty. The functions of smell include environmental detection, food seeking, danger reporting, defense, nourishment, and relation to procreation. Males use smell to recognize females; animals that are not good at smelling do not reproduce well. Therefore, smell and love are like two wheels of a cart, or two wings of a bird, inseparable for even a moment. Now, allow me to finish discussing the bodily odors of women, which vary greatly according to their ethnicity, age, and individuality. There are goat-like smells, dried fruit smells, garlic smells, butyric acid smells, musk smells, and so on. Xi Shi, Yang Guifei, Jieyu, Xun Ling, and Xiang Fei were favored by emperors and nobles because their bodily fragrances were alluring. Those with body odor, even close friends and relatives, would be avoided and shunned, making it a major cause of estrangement and divorce. Furthermore, the bodily odor of celibate men is stronger than that of ordinary people. Some people use this to discern their chastity. Women's sense of smell is particularly well-developed during adolescence, and nosebleeds often occur during this period. Hence, the Western saying: "A nosebleed in youth is a sign of love." Strange smells from the nostrils, sneezing, and colds often erupt with the excitement of love. Leather smells can increase love and abnormal psychology between the sexes. There are many records of this. People are often moved by the shoes they love, likely because shoes are mostly made of leather; loving shoes is a disguised form of loving leather smells. Why do humans uniquely love leather smells? A certain psychologist said it's because it resembles their own odor. Floral fragrances are quick to evoke emotions. White flowers like gardenias, tuberoses, and lilies have the greatest power. Therefore, gifting flowers is an indispensable page in the history of romance. Women often close their eyes and deeply inhale the fragrance of their beloved flowers, lingering with affection.

Arthur Conan Doyle is Dead by Yu Ying 185

The famous British novelist Arthur Conan Doyle, known for his detective novels, wrote over a hundred detective stories featuring Sherlock Holmes. All of them are widely popular and translated into more than ten languages. Many in China's literary circles have also translated his works. His fame is such that anyone who reads detective novels is sure to know him. Unfortunately, bad news has arrived. It is reported that Mr. Doyle passed away at 9:15 AM on the 7th of this month (Monday) at his private residence in Crowborough due to illness. Upon hearing this tragic news, the entire literary world mourned. It is said that Mr. Doyle's illness was caused by lecturing on spiritualism in Denmark, Norway, and Sweden last year. The prolonged effort led to illness, and his condition gradually worsened starting in early November last year. Unexpectedly, he never recovered. Mr. Doyle is survived by his wife and two children.

Reluctant to let go, as if facing a loved one. However, tuberoses, lilacs, irises, and other flowers can injure the voice, even causing muteness. A message to lovers: love flowers in moderation. Observe the orange blossom bouquet held by the bride, mixed with gardenias; its purpose is none other than to use the mixing effect of smells to reduce the intensity of the fragrance. The most beloved fragrance in the world is undoubtedly musk, likely because it closely resembles body odor and sexual odor. Musk itself is taken from the sexual organs of male musk deer. Persians use it to apply to their beards and foreheads to win praise. Muhammad had three loves: women, bodily fragrance and musk, and food. In our country, using musk to scent quilts is considered the ultimate luxury. Humans also have subjective likes and dislikes regarding smell. To a lover, even unpleasant smells are fragrant; to an enemy, even pleasant smells are foul. Breast milk originally has no fragrance, but a lover perceives it as fragrant. Foot odor is originally very foul, but a lover does not notice it. Could this be what is meant by "Words from the same heart have a fragrance like orchids"?

A Returnee from the Front Lines Speaks by Zhuang Yan 186

Yesterday, I met a certain gentleman at a friend's place who had just returned from the front lines of the Longhai Railway. We discussed several interesting matters, which I will recount as follows.

The First Teaching Division fought extremely hard in the front lines this time. During the siege of Gui De's Wan Xuan Cai's troops last month, they used bamboo ladders to climb the city walls. Wan's troops threw bombs from the top of the walls, causing many deaths, but they were ultimately scaled. Wan's captured troops told people that they were still terrified of the valiant soldiers in green uniforms, given their battle record. Once, the division discovered a deserter selling his weapons. He was later captured in Xuzhou and was about to be executed according to military law. However, Commander-in-Chief Chiang saw him and wondered how the Teaching Division could have such a cowardly soldier. He summoned him and asked. The man candidly replied, "I went to the front lines to fight, but my elderly mother at home was on the verge of starvation, as indicated in her urgent letter. I really couldn't bear to sit idly by. Therefore, I sold my weapons to get money to send home. Afterward, I still returned to the front lines to serve. Who would have thought I'd be arrested in Xuzhou?" Chiang heard this and was moved to pity, immediately pardoning his crime and ordering him to return to his unit.

Two soldiers from a certain regiment of the Teaching Division went to the regimental commander's office one day to request their pay. The regimental commander refused, saying there were no funds. They begged repeatedly, but still did not receive a positive response. The two soldiers resolutely said, "We are fighting against the rebels this time with the determination to die. Now, our families are eagerly awaiting pay, as urgent as a burning fire. According to military regulations, each dead soldier can receive twenty yuan in burial expenses. Why doesn't the regimental commander advance this amount to us? In the future, if we die in battle, we are willing to have our corpses exposed without burial." The regimental commander had no choice but to reluctantly agree.

The Central Army treats prisoners of war quite generously. Those who surrender their weapons are all spared death. The Northwest Army, on the other hand, is more harsh. The northerners are straightforward and kill enemies on sight, without regard for humanity or inhumanity. However, there are exceptions. Once, during a battle in Lanfeng, a groom mistakenly led his horse into enemy territory and was captured. He was taken to the division commander, who gave him thirty yuan and two large "heimo" (steamed buns), releasing him to return. He also cautioned him, "Don't eat all the 'heimo'. Leave a little to give to your comrades in the camp so they know the food here is good." The groom was delighted and raced back. He did indeed leave a little "heimo", but most of the Central Army were southerners, unaccustomed to wheat-based foods, and they all vomited after eating it.

The Nameless Sacrifices in the Great Rivers by Lan Huang

Eastern Travel Impressions (5) by Qian Hua 187

(5) Words from a Rickshaw Puller

In recent times, Japan has been advancing rapidly in all aspects. Its material civilization is on par with Europe and America. However, the living standards of its common people have also been steadily increasing. Along the way, I spoke with a rickshaw puller and inquired about his living conditions in detail. His answers were quite interesting and sufficient to glimpse the truth about Japan's lower class. Therefore, I will briefly recount them. The rickshaw puller said, "After graduating from higher elementary school, I joined a labor union due to difficulty in finding employment. I rely on running and physical labor to earn a wage, which is barely enough to support my family. My average income is about two or three yen per day, totaling over sixty or seventy yen per month (Japanese currency). After paying the rickshaw rental, there is still some surplus for household expenses. I set aside a portion for my children's education because I deeply understand the pain of making a living without education. I am determined to provide my children with a full education so they can obtain better positions in society in the future. During the spring, various international groups come to visit. There are several groups touring throughout the month, passing through Nagasaki and sightseeing all over the city. Our income also increases sharply, averaging over a hundred yen per month. Then, we can also prepare for winter clothing. Although our profession is difficult, the domestic politics are enlightened, and local officials are dutiful. They provide various conveniences for the lives of the poor and can solve the problems of food and accommodation in the most economical way, obtaining considerable comfort. Therefore, what I earn from running around all day is used to support my wife and children. At night, the family gathers together to talk, with no worries about accidents. Its joy is indeed harmonious. (People of the country, listen!) Guests like you come from afar, traveling freely throughout Japan, which is very enviable. I live within the country but have only heard of the prosperity of Tokyo. For decades, I have never set foot there. It is truly the biggest regret of my life. With the convenience of transportation in Japan today, traveling between Kyoto and Osaka is as easy as lifting a foot. However, constrained by economic difficulties, my heart has the will, but my strength is insufficient. I don't know how many others in the country share the same plight as me. My only hope today is that my children will strive to improve their abilities in the future and earn a better monthly income, perhaps enough to fulfill my long-cherished wish to visit Tokyo. My eldest son is already eighteen years old and studying at the middle school in our town. If he works hard, it will not be difficult to enter university. Then, my later years can be spent leisurely, avoiding the life of a beast of burden." When the rickshaw puller spoke, his eyebrows danced, and boundless hope overflowed from his words. His far-sightedness is particularly commendable, and we should also express our utmost sympathy for his suffering under economic pressure. The living expenses of a rickshaw puller require sixty to seventy yen per month, which is equivalent to about one hundred and twenty yuan in national currency. The high cost of living can be imagined, and Nagasaki is not comparable to a metropolis. It is said that rickshaw pullers in Tokyo earn about one hundred and fifty yen per month, which is barely enough to cover expenses, incomparable to our country.

The Evil Shanghai has the Great Jiangxi Road and the surging waves of the Huangpu River with its passing sails, a Great River that takes physical form. The flower associations, roulette gambling, and gold exchanges are sources of ruin and disgrace. These three are the Great Rivers without form. Everyone knows that many commit suicide in the Great Rivers of physical form, but they do not know that even more are sacrificed in the Great Rivers without form. Gripping my pen here, I can't help but sigh and weep. Yesterday, I met my friend Mr. Chen at the exchange. He told me about a clerk from a money house who went mad due to a failed speculation last month and was on the verge of death. His causes and consequences are enough to serve as a warning to those blinded by greed and heading down the wrong path. I will record it urgently as follows.

There was a Mr. Zhang, a mid-level clerk in a money house in this city, earning several hundred yuan per year. His family had many members, and expenses always exceeded income, with debts piling up endlessly. In the midst of his helplessness, Mr. Zhang suddenly wanted to try his hand at speculation, hoping for a one-in-a-million chance. Once his plan was decided, he returned to his hometown to beg for help from relatives, gathering a thousand yuan to come to Shanghai. He then entered the gold exchange. The first time, he took a bullish position on one "pong" (seven taels), and the price of gold happened to rise smoothly. For every ten taels the price rose, Zhang increased his bullish position by one "pong." Subsequently, he became too greedy, thinking of becoming a millionaire overnight. Thus, he increased his position by two or three "pongs" every day. Who knew that the winds of change are unpredictable? Within two days, the price of gold suddenly fell from five hundred and thirty taels to five hundred and four taels. Zhang's trustee broker, calculating at this price, found that Zhang's gains were small and his losses were huge. If the price of gold fell further, the risk would be even greater. Therefore, he strongly urged Zhang to settle the price. Zhang, having no funds to maintain his position, tearfully agreed. After the settlement, in addition to the original thousand yuan being confiscated, he still owed two thousand yuan, which the broker advanced. But fate played a cruel joke. The next day, the market opened and suddenly jumped to over five hundred and fifty taels, and within a few days to five hundred and sixty or seventy taels. At this time, Zhang's friend still did not know that he had already settled his position. He called Zhang to congratulate him. Zhang, depressed and resentful for days, was further stimulated by the phone call. Therefore, before releasing the receiver, he fainted and lost consciousness. After being revived, his nerves were deranged, and he went mad. According to the doctor's diagnosis, his life was in danger.

Warmth in the Heart (2)(3)(1) by Bao Tian Xiao 188

Chapter 12: Farewell Banquet, Plucking Flowers to Leave a Charming Impression; Famous Garden Gathering, Tea Tasting to Behold Beautiful Figures

After this World's Fair opened, it indeed caused a sensation for a while. Originally, there were already countless gentlemen and ladies during the cool evenings. Now, everyone wanted to join the excitement even more. Among them, Mr. Shi Guanping was most enthusiastic about charity work, and the initiators of this World's Fair were all old friends. They also grabbed him to be one of the organizers, assigning him the mission of promoting the fair in the newspapers and fulfilling the advertising obligations. At this time, some people also went to persuade the wives and daughters of the wealthy merchants in Shanghai to take out all kinds of precious ornaments to help raise funds. Those ladies and gentlemen were all charitable-minded. They were told how miserable the disaster victims were. "We in Shanghai eat delicacies and live in foreign-style houses. Who knows that they even eat grass roots and bark. Some even eat people. After a disaster victim starves to death, many other disaster victims who have not yet starved to death go to cut off his flesh to eat. It's pitiful that the starved person had mostly bones and little meat left. It was also said, "Your young masters and young ladies are truly enjoying themselves living in Shanghai. If they were in a disaster area, they would be starving to death themselves and would not be able to take care of the children. Two steamed buns can be exchanged for a male child. No one wants female children at all." Speaking of living conditions, drought means barren land for thousands of miles. Floods mean turning everything into marshes. They either live in the wilderness or climb on rooftops." Hearing those words, humans inherently have compassion, especially women, who are more charitable. The old ladies had already been chanting "Amitabha," telling their daughters, "Mr. So-and-so's words are correct. The children of the disaster victims are worthless. Isn't our family's Lai Xi bought from Henan by your grandfather for ten yuan?" This time, the goal was to have the families of Shanghai's wealthy and powerful people donate a little of their remaining precious ornaments. Gathering small amounts can also become a large sum. But to sell so many precious ornaments immediately would be a bit difficult and also a bit uneconomical. So they came up with a method: making a kind of charity lottery ticket called "Planting Blessing Tickets," where every ticket had a prize. On the third day of the World's Fair, the lottery would be drawn in public at An Kai Di. A few days in advance, all kinds of lottery items were displayed in the venue, indicating that the top prize was those kinds of items, the second prize was those kinds of items, the third prize was those kinds of items, and the remaining prizes from the fourth to the tenth also had gifts. The idea of the "Planting Blessing Tickets" was simply to broadly cultivate blessings. Each ticket was sold for one yuan. In addition to directly selling to guests in the venue, the remaining tickets were distributed to the organizers, asking them to distribute them among their relatives and friends. Some were asked to take two hundred tickets, and some were asked to take three hundred tickets. After taking the tickets, they were not allowed to return them. Even if they couldn't sell them, they were asked to advance the money because those tickets would be useless after the lottery was drawn. Those organizers were all respectable people in Shanghai. They didn't care about two or three hundred yuan.

Gold Market Suddenly Reverses Course 189

Rebounding Nine Taels and Three Mace

Turning from Weak to Strong, Market Shows Promising Signs. Yesterday, the 12th, the gold market turned from weak to strong, breaking through the 600 tael mark. Market sentiment was auspicious, and prices steadily increased, fluctuating by only two or three taels at the start. However, the difference eventually reached thirteen taels. Foreign exchange showed a slight increase, and market trading was relatively brisk. Buyers took the upper hand, mainly due to the continuous rise in cash prices. The August benchmark gold price required a premium of thirteen or fourteen taels, and there were many eager buyers. For bars, Fuchangxiang, Yuyu, Dafuxing, Yongzhifeng, etc., all increased their positions. Yuanxingyong and Yuanmaoyong repurchased after selling, while Yifengyong, Yongchengchang, and Wanxing, etc., all sold. Early in the day, large bars increased in price, then weakened, hovering around ninety taels. Later, buyers became very active, and prices soared. By midday, they suddenly jumped by more than ten taels, breaking through 602 taels quickly. Because it was Saturday, the market closed as usual. Yesterday, the price of spot British silver increased by another one-sixteenth, while forward prices remained unchanged. The price of silver also increased by one-quarter, and the exchange rate suddenly decreased by one-sixteenth.

In the end, it broke through the 600 tael mark. The opening price for August gold fell by 2.2 mace to 590 taels and 2 mace. Later, it rose from 89.8 mace to 94.2 mace, and Fuchangxiang, Yuyu, etc., bought in. The exchange rate remained stable. The spot price for Japanese gold, bought by Mitsui, increased by 1.33125 shillings. When the notice for the spot price was posted, it decreased slightly by 2 mace, calculated at 92.12 mace. However, the listed exchange rates did not move and immediately rebounded by 1 mace. Afterward, it gradually increased. The September British gold for Andahua and Bi Mutual traded at 6 pence and 375 mils, so the price of gold rose by three or four mace to 97.5 mace at 10 o'clock. Shortly after, it decreased slightly by 2 mace to 95.3 mace. Retail investors sold, and because buyers were persistent, it still rose to 97.23 mace. After 10:30, Yifengyong, Xieyu, Yucheng Yong, etc., showed a strong intention to sell, seeming to be heading downward. It dropped by more than 2 mace, calculated at 94.89 mace. Korea sold August British gold for 6 pence and 25 mils. However, the exchange rate trading was quiet. After a while, retail investors, etc., sold, and it immediately depreciated by 1 mace, amounting to 599 taels and 56 mace. People's confidence was extremely strong, and those who had sold previously rushed to buy back, so there was even more demand on the trading floor. It had already risen by more than 2 mace, reaching 601 taels and 9 mace at noon. At noon, it closed at 601 taels and 7 mace, and then it rose by a few more mace, increasing by 9.3 mace compared to yesterday. This was a rebound after many days of decline.

The lowest settlement price was Yichang at 52 taels. British and American Silver Prices Continue to Rise 191

Wavy Rise in Silver Dollar Prices 192

Market Overview: The current trend of silver dollar prices, considering the time of year, suggests that the slack season of summer makes any thorough rise unlikely. However, the needs of the various ports and cities show such a demand that there is indeed a reason for prices to rise. Therefore, these two opposing situations have converged to form a wavy pattern in the current state of silver dollar prices, with particularly large fluctuations. In the past few days, the overall pattern has been a drop in the morning and a rise in the afternoon, with the result of a daily increase of a certain number of notches. New highs not seen this year have repeatedly appeared. Although there is no direct skyrocketing, the incremental increase in the wavy pattern cannot be underestimated.

Silver Dollar Swap Prices (Silver Dollar): Trading was still active in the morning, but the balance of supply and demand resulted in a silver dollar price that fell by 1 hao and 2 hu compared to the previous noon, to 7 jiao, 2 fen, 5 li, 8 hao, and 7 hu and a half. Unexpectedly, market sentiment was revived at noon, and prices surged. The listed price was once as high as 7 jiao, 2 fen, and 8 li. The closing price was 7 jiao, 2 fen, 6 li, and 7 hao and a half, an increase of 8 hao and 7 hu and a half compared to the previous noon, and also a new high for this year. (Silver Swap): The market was slightly bullish yesterday. The morning market was still 8 fen, and the noon market opened at 1 qian. Additional water was still 2-3 fen. The banks did not list prices, and the silver market seemed to be slightly better than the previous day.

Subsidiary Coin Market: The price of Jiangnan small silver dollars increased slightly by 1 li compared to the previous day, with both markets at 6 qian, 3 fen, and 1 li. Only 3,000 jiao were transacted in the morning market. However, the rising trend of Guangdong small silver dollars was even stronger. The morning market soared to 6 qian and 09 li, an increase of 4 li compared to the previous morning. The noon market continued to rise by more than 2 li, exceeding the 1 fen mark, to 6 qian, 1 fen, 1 li, and 2 hao and a half. The future looks very strong. Transactions amounted to 175 million jiao in the morning market and 100.5 million jiao in the noon market. There was still a demand. Copper coins also decreased by 4,000, to 384,000 wen, the lowest price seen recently.

Inflow and Outflow of Silver Dollars (Silver Coins): Yesterday was Saturday, and the banks' collection and release were as quiet as usual. Chinese merchants collected and released 1.12 million yuan, foreign merchants collected and released 1.78 million yuan, and various goods, exchange rates, taxes, and miscellaneous payments collected and released 7.89 million yuan. Cotton Yarn Market Struggles to Progress 194

Global cotton yarn prices decline, spot sales are sluggish.

The yarn market is weakening, mainly because the global cotton yarn market is trending downward, causing market sentiment to suddenly weaken. However, buyers remain calm and show no signs of loosening their stance. Spot yarn sales are becoming increasingly slow, and business from Guangdong merchants is also lacking. One yarn factory is selling off large quantities, with approximately 5,000 to 6,000 bales traded in both the morning and afternoon sessions. However, the market trend has remained strong in recent months due to the peak season. The situation for far-month foreign cotton is unfavorable, with more short selling, it is said.

The entire factory sold off 5,000-6,000 pieces of bid yarn. At the exchange, the morning session opened with weakening market sentiment due to declining American cotton prices, and Hou Sheng Factory dumped yarn, causing prices for all months to drop by 1.5, 6, or 7 yuan. In the afternoon, some traders took profits by covering short positions, slightly strengthening the market, with prices for all months rising or falling by 1 or 2 yuan. The total transaction volume for the day was 12,650 bales. Public Tai, Shen Yu, Tian Chang, Yi Cheng, Da Ji, and Chang Feng sold 300 to 1,600 bales each, while He Shen, Yu Da, Tian Cheng, Bao Chang, Xie Sheng, Da Feng, Tian Long, and Yi Long bought 250 to 1,000 bales each. American Cotton Started Weak Last Week and Then Strengthened 197

Government Report Estimates Cotton Acreage Reduced by 2.7%

Most cotton-growing areas currently need rain, and bollworm reproduction has decreased.

A New York telegram dated the 11th reports on the cotton market for the past week: The cotton market started weak last week but then strengthened following the government report. The government estimates that cotton acreage has decreased by approximately 2.7% compared to last year. After the report, local merchants and bankers sold off slightly, but when the October contract price reached 12.5 cents, the supply was absorbed. Subsequently, due to the better actual situation and excessively high temperatures in the cotton-growing areas, the market slightly improved. Although the current dryness is not yet sufficient to harm the new cotton, it is believed that most areas in the South need rain. At the same time, industry insiders expect the average production to increase, as bollworm damage has decreased on average. Private reports indicate that bollworm reproduction has decreased significantly compared to last year. The weekend statistics are attached on the left (units in thousands of bales):

85,000 Bags of Foreign Rice Arrive Again 198

Demand from inland areas of this city is not weak... Prices rebound by 0.30 yuan.

Yesterday, a new ship carrying 85,000 bags of foreign rice arrived. Including the previous stock, there are now close to 1 million bags. However, the ship "Mingyu Maru" that arrived yesterday was one of the last shipments of fixed orders. After this, except for new orders, all previously fixed orders have been fulfilled. Yesterday, the market saw avenues for sales in the inland areas of this city and flat sales. Market sentiment turned positive, and many speculators were interested, leading to a rebound of 0.20 or 0.30 yuan for various types of rice. Flour Market Shows Signs of Near-Term Stability and Long-Term Weakness 199

Wheat Continues to Fall by 0.60 to 0.70 Yuan... Market Sentiment in This City Turns Soft

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning and afternoon, prices for various months showed signs of near-term stability and long-term weakness. Although actual sales for the current month are not very smooth, the inventories of the factories are not abundant (the fact that spot flour must be priced according to the standard is clear evidence). Therefore, market sentiment in each session remained calm. As for the distant months, the quoted price of wheat continued to fall by 0.60 to 0.70 yuan. Generally, people expect that if the exchange rate can be further lengthened when the price of foreign wheat falls, the market value between Chinese and foreign wheat may become more reasonable. Therefore, market sentiment is quite weak. However, inland hoarders continue to absorb wheat, and short covering is also very strong, so the market has not seen a huge decline. Looking at the future situation, the bad environment may lead to stagnation. As a result, the current month remained unchanged, August fell by 0.05 yuan, September fell by 0.075 yuan, and November and December fell by 0.05 yuan, it is said.

Factory Sales of Long-Term Wheat Plummet 200

Factory appetite for spot wheat is not open, and inventories continue to increase... Prices of new and old wheat fall by a few coins

Yesterday, after the opening of the futures wheat market in the morning and afternoon, prices for various months showed a trend of near-term stability and long-term decline. Since the current month is unrelated and the market prices in various producing areas have not been greatly reduced, the factory appetite is not good, but market sentiment can still be stabilized. As for the distant months, brokers close to the factories and some factories continue to sell off sharply, causing the market in each session to plummet. However, the Suzhou gang saw the price of inland wheat rise sharply and bought in large quantities. Unfortunately, the situation is extraordinary and cannot be sustained. As a result, the current month remained unchanged, while August to October fell by 0.04 yuan each, November fell by 0.06 yuan, and December fell by 0.05 yuan. Spot wheat market conditions are such that factories unanimously hold back and are unwilling to take advantage, causing inventories to increase. Many people are trying to sell off, so prices for new and old wheat have fallen by about a few coins. More than 3,000 bags of Kaihuangqiao, Zhumadian, and Xuzhou old wheat were purchased by various factories, it is said.

Prices of North-South Goods and White Lotus Seeds Soar 201

Land prices rise by 12 yuan... Shanghai prices also increase by 5 to 6 taels

Recently, the white lotus seed market has been particularly tight due to the rise in land prices. The previous purchase price was only 40 yuan, but now it has risen to 52 yuan, an increase of more than 12 yuan. At this price, the Shanghai standard is around 42 taels, which is difficult to match. Therefore, the source is extremely scarce. The previous sales price here was 33 to 34 taels, but it has gradually risen to 38 taels. Yesterday, the quoted price was 40 taels, which is still cheaper than the land price, so the market may rise again, it is feared.

Qingfeng Garden 212

How Many Words Can We Really Use?

Talking, reading, and writing are things that people cannot leave every day, especially the former, which is needed by barbarians and young children. The tool for doing these things is undoubtedly the (word), but we have to think about how many words we can really use.

Regarding this point, Westerners have many interesting statistics. In 1860, Oxford University Professor Max Muller said in a speech that a British rural farmer skillfully used at most 300 words, but according to Dr. Kail Lokotsch, this statement is not difficult to refute today. He collected many novel things to refute Professor Muller's statement. The following are his words:

Mrs. Winneld SHall of the United States recorded the words spoken by her young children from the beginning of speaking. By the seventeenth month, the child used 232 different words, which increased to 2,688 words by the age of six.

This can only be regarded as a minimum number, because children always have many words that escape the records of their mothers and nannies.

German linguist Wundt also did the same experiment. He experimented that a two-year-old girl used 489 words, and a girl of the same age used as many as 1,128 words.

Therefore, Professor MMuller's statement is absurd. No adult uses fewer words than a two-year-old child. Moreover, farmers cannot but know many special agricultural words. Even the simplest farmer cannot live on 300 words.

An average person who has received eight years of general education in school and usually reads magazines, newspapers, and listens to radio lectures, etc., has a vocabulary of at least 10,000 or more.

But people who have received higher education are even more different.

Professor E.S. Hlolden once selected the words he knew in Webster's University Dictionary, which totaled 33,456 words. Mr. E.H. Babbitt experimented with his students, and most of the students knew no less than 60,000 words, which is even more amazing.

But we must know that recognizing words and using words are very different. Even if the words recognized are very many, only a few of them are used, especially in writing. This can be proven by the following example. This is Miss Liu Wofei, the daughter of Mr. Liu Yazi, the best graduate of the Preparatory Department of Datong University (photographed by Ye Changlie)

(The Iliad) and (The Odyssey) used a total of only 9,000 different words. Shakespeare, the writer with the richest vocabulary, used only about 20,000 words in all his works.

This is the situation of word usage among European and American cultural people. Let's take a look at the situation of many semi-uncivilized people.

Many primitive peoples have a surprising number of words. The 1550 Mexican Aztec dictionary already had 13,000 words. One investigator found that the Yaarans race, who did not even know about coats and trousers, used 30,000 words. The most amazing thing is the vocabulary of the Arabs. They have a hundred different words for calling camels, five hundred different words for calling awls, and a thousand different words for calling a sword. Everyone can imagine how vast the Arabic dictionary is.

The Sorrow After Marriage Quiet 213

Because of the proof of reality, she had to believe that marriage was the graveyard of love. Now, all she could obtain was boredom and sorrow. She regretted it; she regretted hurrying into marriage with him and driving away the sweetness and beauty of their love. Moreover, burying it deeply and forever in the grave; how could this not make her feel an unusual sorrow?

She recalled the pleasant past, the sweetness of life, and unconsciously revealed a slight smile. But reality followed, disturbing her. The smile of a fleeting moment would immediately be withdrawn, returning to the state where she only felt emptiness and loneliness. Her brows furrowed with vexation, tightly wrinkled, hating even more the demon that controlled reality. She unconsciously let out a breath and exclaimed, "Mother, is married life like this? Can it really become so unbearable?"

Before marriage, how happy she was! Not only were passersby envious, but all the relatives and friends who knew them were praising them, gazing with envious eyes. Even she herself was very satisfied, self-proud, and thought that the god of love was especially kind to her.

Not long after the marriage, naturally, it was still as ardent as before marriage, and even more joyful than before marriage; it was truly more than enough. But what was hateful was that the angel who governs love was no different from the gods who govern other destinies. It too wanted to make fun of people, especially those who would not escape the general rule that extreme prosperity must decline. Now, two years after marriage, all she could enjoy was the innocent laughter of her beloved daughter. Where had the deep affection of her beloved gone? Where had it gone? Some said that the innocent laughter of her beloved daughter was the price of sacrificing the deep affection of her beloved. Was it true? Was it really sent to pay the price for the innocent laughter of her beloved daughter? Thinking of this, her vision blurred, as if she had lost a treasure, a treasure that was forever difficult to regain, forcing her to feel heartbroken and to wipe away her tears silently.

After being heartbroken, watching her beloved daughter sleeping in the cradle, sleeping very quietly, she picked up paper and pen and wrote a letter to her friend of many years, saying, "If this is a letter, it is naturally not as poignant as calling it a lament after marriage." Below is the letter she wrote:

Yun Yao, dear friend, I am so grateful that you wrote two letters from afar to ask about my illness. At that time, I was ill, and furthermore, Qin'er was constantly pestering me. I really had no time, so I did not write back. Please forgive me. I believe you will understand me.

Good friend, how troubled is my heart now. This illness of mine was certainly caused by postpartum weakness, but it can also be said to have arisen from vexation. Because between my husband and I, there has arisen a secret pain.

What is my vexation? To be honest, it is that my husband's love for me has gradually faded recently. Compared to the love at the beginning of our marriage, it is truly like a gulf.

He truly cannot forgive me. He says that the love I give him now is not as ardent and profound as before, and I am not willing to give love wholeheartedly. This is truly wronging me! I wish I could take out my heart and show it to him carefully. Only let the god of love know my heart! He even said that I only know how to fully express maternal love and have left him aside. But, Sister Yao, you must know that when a woman has children, she wants to express maternal love; this is an expression of her nature. How can he resent me? Of course, I also know that in this kind of situation, a man, whether he understands it or not, will naturally always feel strange and lonely. But I also have no way to deal with it.

In reality, isn't he himself also changing? How often is he exerting his utmost to give love? In short, what I feel now is only mediocrity and loneliness. Fortunately, sometimes teasing the innocent laughter of this little thing will make me forget everything. If it weren't for Qin'er constantly entertaining me, I don't know how unbearable I would feel. Sister Yao, dear Sister Yao, do you think I am very happy? Do you think I am enjoying the pleasures of life to the fullest? Please see for yourself whether the married life I am enjoying is the pleasure of life or hell on earth. It is truly enough for me to enjoy.

Let me tell you, marriage is the hardening of love, but if one can prevent it, one can still maintain the delicate and deep feelings of the past. Sister Yao, although I know this, I cannot put it into practice. I don't even know how to put it into practice. Therefore, our encounters can only be in the stifling, lonely sorrow, only feeling an unusual boredom and mediocrity..."

Oh, my little baby is squirming. It's probably about to wake up. I can't write to you much longer. The myriad sorrows and the countless grievances can only be left for another opportunity to talk to you to my heart's content. (Omitted below)
