Book Review

The Source of Disease and Treatment for the Chinese Nation by Zhi Jing, Gao Huaichuan 214

The decline of the Chinese national character, the Chinese nation's disease reaching the bone marrow, suffering from the poisonous roots of two thousand years to the point of being bedridden and lingering with only a breath left. At this moment, some people still say that the large Chinese nation is not afraid of being conquered by other nations, and even if it were conquered, it would assimilate them. Furthermore, some even have sores all over their bodies and still say that they are not sick. This is truly laughable and pitiful. Because of this concept, they fundamentally do not admit that the Chinese nation is sick, and naturally they do not investigate the root of the disease. Then, the question facing us is whether we Chinese have a national concept, and whether we clearly recognize our national consciousness. This is undeniable. The public is like scattered sand, only remembering their own family at all times. What nation or no nation, in their minds, it seems like there is no such thing. The author of "The Source of Disease and Treatment for the Chinese Nation" saw this point, so he frankly used historical facts to prove the incurable situation of the Chinese nation's disease, found the location of the disease, found the root of the disease, and, in accordance with the timing, gave a full dose of stimulant and wrote a good prescription. Such a creation cannot be said to be unprecedented, nor can it be called a pearl in every word, but in the modern Chinese nation, which has been poisoned for a long time and whose disease has reached the bone marrow, I feel that it is necessary to expose its shortcomings and find the crux of its decline.

The book is divided into sixteen chapters. As usual, the first chapter is the introduction, which describes the general views on the cause of the disease. Some say it is the relationship of the clan system, some say it is the geographical relationship, some say it is the political system, some say it is the academic relationship, etc. The author believes that they cannot be said to be completely wrong, and that they are all related to the weakening of China. However, "if we designate these few as the causes of weakening without attaching conditions, in fact, there is something wrong, and theoretically, of course, it is even more untenable. Therefore, I believe that the weakening of China must have another kind of thing interfering from within." Regarding this kind of interference, let's see what he says: "The weakening of China, as seen from historical events, is indeed a part of the responsibility that has developed a defect. The reason for the defect in responsibility is that a part is sick. Its function breaks away from responsibility, and instead is driven by the disease to promote the disease. After years of accumulation, it has created a 'sick man of East Asia'."

Therefore, in the second part of his work, he tries his best to expose the truth about this part of the responsibility that has developed a defect. He vehemently rebukes the Chinese scholars, who from the Han Dynasty onwards have dreamed of nothing but becoming officials. Wanting to be an official is naturally not a bad thing, but the intentions of this group of scholars who want to become officials are somewhat special. "Upon careful examination, what they want is the authority of the official, the dignity of the official, the prosperity of the official. Becoming an official can be fulfilling, can be comfortable, can be indulgent, can be for personal gain. Thinking of the official for one's own convenience, thinking of the official for one's own happiness. It is not to study politics and use the responsibility of politics that they want to become an official. Inside the official, there is also something particularly bad, which is getting rich. Once rich, one can have abundant food and clothing, and can have proud wives and beautiful concubines, and even have wealth that continues for generations. Where there is profit, people tend to flock to it. Therefore, the two words 'getting rich' have increased the heat of their desire to become officials by hundreds of times. When their psychological function reaches this level, naturally there is no talk of the responsibility of the official. How politics is studied, he does not ask. How politics is used, he does not care. He simply believes that reading is a tool for seeking office, and being an official is the reward for reading. Reading to seek office, and obtaining office because of reading. Reading is the cause of becoming an official, and becoming an official is the result of reading. Reading until one becomes an official is considered a good cause and a good result, and one can face the heavens and tell people, and there is no slightest regret or subtle defect.

Then, the author discusses the defect in the responsibility of Chinese officials. Based on historical facts, his conclusion is that "officials before the Duke of Zhou were responsible. Officials in the era of the Warring States were incompetent to take responsibility and had to rely on their personal identity. Officials in the Western Han Dynasty were focused on negative responsibility, discarding positive responsibility. Officials after the end of the Han Dynasty not only discarded positive responsibility, but also discarded negative responsibility completely. Not only negative responsibility, but also their personal identity was sacrificed, willingly acting as a tool of the emperor. If a person reaches the point of disregarding their identity, naturally they will go downhill day by day, and there is nothing brilliant to say. Therefore, the officials after the Jin Dynasty simply wanted the vanity of being an official and the actual benefits of money. Not to mention that the identity of the officials became unspeakably bad, but also the ability and knowledge of the officials themselves decreased day by day. By the late Song and Ming Dynasties, the government offices of those officials had almost become a home for the disabled. If everyone doesn't believe it, please look at how they treated the Jin, Yuan, and Qing invasions, and you will understand. Naturally, they could not but explore the secret to seeking office, could not but study the method of being an official, and even more could not but search for the way to make money. So it came to the point that all the high officials (could not govern the country in peacetime and could not respond to changes in times of chaos. We look at the Song Dynasty, which was uncertain about peace and war and full of debate, and the Ming Dynasty, which was noisy when things were urgent and noisy when things were slow, and we can know their tricks. Local officials were less intelligent than merchants and less knowledgeable than clerks. We look at those who do not distinguish between the plaintiff and the defendant in the courtroom and do not distinguish between wheat and rice in the fields, and we can also prove their knowledge.) Regarding the welfare of the people, they did not care at all, and simply became an obligation to pay money and a right to ask for money. How much less did they care about the cultivation of national character?

Secondly, the author talks about the defect in the responsibility of Chinese soldiers. In the Chinese social psychology of "good iron is not used to make nails, and good people do not become soldiers," the recruits are naturally not good elements. They are all poor and lazy hooligans. Forced by life, they have to take risks. So, they all gather under a recruiting banner without prior consultation. "So it came to the point that the organization of the army completely became a collection of poor people, lazy people, and violent people. Once they are about to set out for battle, they are also inexplicable as to why. They only hear the superiors issuing an order, calling them to start walking. Then they have no choice but to carry their guns and drag their legs to the front line. When they are hit by bullets and die, they also do not know why they sacrificed. However, they have never seen them being as brave for national wars as they are for private fights. They simply do not know the meaning of being a soldier or the responsibility of being a soldier."

China's diseases are really too many, and the degree of the diseases is deep enough. To summarize in one sentence, it can be said that it is all caused by the affliction of wealth and prosperity. The third part of this book exposes all aspects of China's diseases very thoroughly, truthfully stating the location of the symptoms of the disease. Looking at the historical facts of the past dynasties, it was either established to protect wealth and prosperity or there was strife to seek wealth and prosperity. In the past two thousand years, the changes in the political situation have been sometimes tense and sometimes lax, sometimes moving and sometimes still, none of which did not have wealth and prosperity as the center. "Therefore, no matter what the occasion, there is always a competition for private interests and no achievement of public interest. There is much discussion and little action. There is much seeing and little effort, taking private as private, taking public as private, transforming public into private, and benefiting private interests under the guise of public service. Private methods are everywhere, and everyone can do them." So, it has completely become a social disease.

This is known to everyone, and naturally we cannot allow this terrible social disease to spread. Regarding this point, the author has determined the treatment method and its order. He feels that the defect of the soldiers is like cholera. We must first find a way to prevent this cholera disease, and then come back to talk about the wealth and prosperity disease that has spread for two thousand years. In short, his treatment method is to use preventive measures in the areas of agriculture, industry, and commerce to prevent the disease demon from invading. In the area of scholars, he uses a containment method to cut off the wings of the disease demon. In the area of seeking office, he uses a blocking and suppressing method to cut off the way out for the disease demon. In the area of being an official, he uses a combination of suppression and appeasement methods to eliminate the power of the disease demon and sever the lifeblood of the disease demon. As for the detailed implementation methods, I can only ask the reader to refer to the original book.

In the fourth part, the author tells us about the vitality and new life of China's future. After the Northern Expedition was completed, the period of political tutelage has already begun. Regarding political reform, at least there are some in fact. There is no need to be greedy for more, and there is no need to be far-sighted. We should measure our strength and demand results. If there are no results, then punish. Chinese people are lazy. If the local officials in the future are willing to teach everyone to do it and prevent everyone from not doing it, and if Chinese officials have the bad habit of "wanting money and not doing things," if there is a supervisory court to give those officials some fear, then naturally China's new vitality is hopeful. We should extend our own feelings to others, and after revitalizing our own national character, we can naturally follow Mr. Sun Yat-sen's nationalism and seek the welfare and equality of all nations in the world. Knowing is difficult and doing is easy. I'm just afraid that we haven't completely understood it. If we all clearly recognize our own national character and are willing to work hard, our future is bright and great. At that time, the white sun will be in the sky, and all things will be nurtured, like that cold night moon that serves as a supplement for us.

Unable to escape the common general format, the last part is also, as usual, the conclusion. In the conclusion, he also describes the current situation of external pressure and the location of internal weaknesses, and says that "external pressure is actually caused by internal weaknesses, and internal weaknesses are actually cast by internal diseases." Therefore, if we want the Chinese nation to be healthy, we should work hard to remove the diseases of laziness and cynicism. We should also correct our wrong consciousness and enrich our inherent beautiful national character.

It is not that I intentionally nitpick. I really feel that there are some imperfections. Regarding the aspects of China's diseases, what the author has reported are all about the literate class. As for the will of the common people, who make up the majority of the Chinese nation, there is no exposure of some defects, which seems to be not without shortcomings. I am not trying to shift the sins of the officials and scholars onto the majority of the common people. The sins of the officials and scholars are a fact. At the same time, the ignorance of the common people, which leads to the decline of the entire nation, also seems to be a defect. This is also a fact. I feel that the majority of the common people are indeed pitiful. They do not know that there is such a thing as "nation," and therefore do not know that they are Chinese, and naturally do not recognize their own national consciousness. Being subjected to double oppression and exploitation, they are still willing to suffer a little loss and seek to turn trouble into nothing. How can we ignore this great phenomenon of social pathology without seeking remedies?

There are countries in the world that have perished because of laziness. If we continue to be lazy, I am afraid that we will follow in their footsteps. In this autumn of crisis, can the Chinese nation still not take on the responsibility for the nation? How should we eliminate national pathogens, awaken national consciousness, and consolidate the strength of the Chinese nation?

News of the Sisters by Tang Zengyang 215

By Xu Helin

Modern young people are all infected with a so-called disease of the century, constantly experiencing the stimulation of misfortune, and thus becoming decadent. As a result, they seek unexpected comfort in the literary and artistic realm that can reconcile their dry lives. This is the so-called only way to seek comfort in life. Moreover, the cries evoked from one's own passionate heart feel particularly real and interesting, and can be regarded as a memento left over from the life process. This alone makes it not meaningless for a young literary artist to vent his own creative desires. Mr. Xu Helin wrote "News of the Sisters" and left it for the world to see for this reason.

However, Mr. Xu's moans from his heart can easily arouse the sympathy of our readers, as if the author has faithfully written down in words the unfortunate experiences that we want to express, nakedly and completely. The minds that have been frequently struck by the same golden arrow also gain a trace of (the comfort and joy that ordinary humans and the ordinary universe cannot give me). This is because the author's narrative is true and not false.

A small collection that encompasses content that can resonate with readers and at the same time provide a kind of unobtainable comfort is truly rare and valuable. However, the author of this book has actually managed to do this, so I believe that there must be many people who (share feelings) with the author, then it is necessary to inquire about this "News of the Sisters".

The entire book is only one hundred and six pages long and includes seven short stories: 1. News of the Sisters, 2. The Pitiful Evening Party, 3. Comedy on West Lake, 4. New Awakening, 5. Small Stain, 6. Donkey's Whining, 7. Good Encounter. These contain both the news and stories of women, so naming it "News of the Sisters" is very appropriate. Essays such as "The Pitiful Evening Party" depict "the victory of women" with great insight, expressing the true meaning of love with artistic skill, allowing us to taste (the taste of love) while reading.

The author's depiction of the female psychology is particularly skillful, sometimes tense, sometimes relaxed, sometimes delicate, sometimes crude, as if he had dug the woman's heart out of her chest and placed it before the public's eyes, making it clearer than anything else.

The intelligent Yingying immediately understood that this was his extravagant wish and secret thoughts for her future. Although she was very willing to agree to this truly moving request, at this moment, in order to maintain the dignity of the spirit when people first meet, it was necessary to deliberately say a few evasive words to avoid the direct attack of this emotion. She pretended not to have heard clearly and hurriedly replied, "We have traveled together three or four times before, yes.

But in the past, many people came together." (Page 44)

After reading this short paragraph in "Comedy on West Lake", we can understand that the author's portrayal of women's psychology and attitude is very vivid, as if we have seen the entire woman's heart. Such powerful depiction is indeed worthy of envy, and it is rare in many creative books. At the same time, perhaps the author also has a considerable study of women's issues, otherwise, his writing about women would not be so flexible and vivid no matter what.

(No, no, I swear to my conscience, I love you and I love the children, but I can't help but love myself. This is my new awakening since last night.)

(Of course, it is an awakening for me, of course it is a very new awakening. If I never had this awakening, my life would eventually be shattered under the burden of a good mother and a virtuous wife, and no one would care...) (Page 62) In the above two very simple dialogues, the family problems between the two sexes and the so-called (good mother and virtuous wife) concept left over from the old society can be clearly seen. This is also evidence that the author has a considerable study of women's issues. In the essay "New Awakening", he also nakedly exposed the male's contempt and bullying of women, as well as the sinister intentions hidden in their hearts.

(...All my youth, all my youthful energy, all my youthful appearance, all my youthful hopes, all my youthful poetic inspiration have been ruined, buried, and sacrificed by you, but you often look at me with sharp eyes, looking at the children, looking at the family, looking at life and society, and often take a proud attitude towards me, towards the children, towards the family, towards life and society. Alas, your thoughts are rotting little by little, and you don't even know that the inferior roots of suppressing women, which have been passed down from your ancestors and hidden in the inheritance of your jade body, are erupting little by little. You don't feel it at all. You, you are so pitiful, so ridiculous, so lamentable!) (Page 63)

What meaningful words these are, actually uttered from the mouth of a woman. It is really not easy, and it can be seen that the woman's entire resolute personality is gradually grasping new consciousness and embarking on the road to awakening. Moreover, the author, Mr. Xu, has also grasped some of the national consciousness, but he starts from the family, and this component is very small.

This is really because our families before today are unreasonable, unorganized, and sick, and are doomed to failure. If we insist on maintaining and perfunctorily continuing such a family that you and I both feel dissatisfied with, isn't it very dangerous? Isn't it more painful? We are not a French-style (out of sight, out of mind) nation. In fact, the sweetness of our love will become more intense because of (out of sight)...

It is inevitable that the author has this kind of consciousness, because he powerfully expresses the personality of Chinese women, which can also be regarded as promoting the spirit of the nation, especially the description of various phenomena in Chinese new and old families. However, this is not yet an aggressive and active one, it can only represent that he has grasped some superficial national consciousness.

The essay "News of the Sisters" is a story woven from ten letters, but when read consecutively, it also has considerable significance, unlike the usual popular and simple love stories that are so boring. It is really because the creation of stories that powerfully depict the female psychology and various events that occur between families is too rare. This is the only point that makes this book worthy of introduction.

Manuscript Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Introductions 216

(1) Limited to introducing the latest publications, domestic and foreign. In addition to literary works, all political, economic, legal, scientific, educational, etc. books and newspapers are included in the introduction, but boring books will not be introduced.

(2) Articles on textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(3) Pictures and photos are limited to those related to the text.

(4) Each article should not exceed 3,000 words.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write manuscripts horizontally, and do not write sloppily. Western texts can be omitted if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw pictures in the manuscript, and use colored paper. Use white paper and black drawings.

European Federation

(1) At the 59th session of the Executive Council of the League of Nations, X in the picture is the chairman, Yugoslav Foreign Minister Linkowiecki, to the left is French Foreign Minister Briand, Italian Foreign Minister Grandi, and German Foreign Minister Curtius, to the right is Secretary-General Drummond, British Foreign Minister Henderson, and Japanese Ambassador to Belgium Nagai Matsuzo, all of whom are permanent members, and the rest are non-permanent members. Due to China's continued weakness, it has repeatedly failed to be elected. If issues related to China are discussed, a special seat will be set up to temporarily invite Chinese representatives to participate. 〇 in the picture is a reporter. The most important event discussed at this meeting was the issue of organizing the European Federation. Regarding our country, it is the issue of cooperation between China and the health organization of the League of Nations.

(2) The picture shows French Foreign Minister Briand, who initiated the organization of the European Federation on the left, and French Prime Minister Tardieu on the right. On September 9th last year, Briand took the opportunity of the League of Nations annual conference to invite representatives of European countries to a luncheon to explain the importance of initiating the organization of the European Federation. At that time, everyone expressed sympathy. The French government conducted further concrete research. On May 17th this year, the French government took advantage of the day when the International Payment Bank officially took over the management of Germany's secret debt and sent out a memorandum on organizing the European Federation. Its superficial reason is that in order to seek European peace, economic cooperation must be carried out. In fact, it arose from the economic pressure exerted by the United States after the European War. As the name suggests, it is known that Europe and the United States are obviously opposed to each other.

(3) The new League of Nations building in Geneva, Sweden is currently under construction. The picture shows the plan designed by architectural experts.

(4) New York City as seen from the U.S. Navy airship, from 40th Street to 57th Street, with the Times Square and Paramount Building as the center, is the area with the tallest buildings and the most prosperous commerce. After the European War, the United States jumped from a debtor nation to a creditor nation, and the world's financial center shifted from London to New York. Therefore, today's New York City is the headquarters of the United States' economic invasion of the world.

(5) Gold is expensive and silver is cheap, and prices are soaring and commerce is stagnant. Our country is a country that uses silver, and it is manipulated by foreigners, and the world's finances are now in the hands of Americans. The fundamental plan should be to change to the gold standard. This is the tense situation in front of the Shanghai Gold Exchange. The government has already restricted the buying and selling of gold speculation.

(6) July 4th is the 154th anniversary of the United States' declaration of independence. On the morning of that day, hundreds of American expatriates in Shanghai brought their children to gather at the U.S. Consul General's Office to participate in the flag-raising ceremony. The picture shows Consul General Cunningham giving a brief speech on the situation in the country.

(7) The protocol of the Sino-Polish Commercial Treaty was formally signed by Wang Zhengting and Polish Plenipotentiary Weydenthal at the Capital Diplomatic Residence at 4:30 pm on July 1st. After the protocol is sent to the Polish government and a telegram is received, it can be announced simultaneously by both parties. The picture shows Minister Wang, Section Chief Xu, Director Hu, Polish Councilor Guo Lei Xinji, and Polish Representative Wei from left to right.

(8) The situation of Japan's chief plenipotentiary representative to the London Naval Conference, Wakatsuki Reijiro, returning to Tokyo and receiving a warm welcome from the people.

Artistic Pursuits

(1) Miss Yu Qingshou is the daughter of Mr. Yu Rizhang. She majored in music at the University of Isaka in the United States and has now completed her studies and returned to China.

(2) Miss Li Mengyan is the granddaughter of Mr. Li Muqi. She is proficient in French. Her assistance was invaluable in the book "East Asian Illness: Flesh and Death." It is a well-known story in literary circles.

(3) Miss Lin Ying is the granddaughter of Mr. Lin Yishu in Southern Fujian. She has a deep family background and has a way in both calligraphy and painting (Guo Feng).

(4) Mr. Shu Zhen is the only Chinese member of the Shanghai Municipal Pony Hyun Orchestra and also the youngest member of the band. He has now founded the Metropolitan Music Store to promote Western music and hopes that his art can spread to the masses.

(5) The Peiping YWCA held a variety show at the annual meeting last month. The members performed an interesting drama, "Grandma Liu Enters the Grand View Garden." This is the main character in the play. On the right is Ms. Li Yaoqing as Ping'er, and on the left is Ms. Yue as Mandarin Duck (Li Yaosheng).

(6) Mrs. Xu Shiqi, Ms. Yang Xuhua, is currently studying music in Europe. She is photographed with a shepherd boy in India. The contrast between black and white is interesting.

(7) Miss Zhang Pingling is a graduate of Jinling Women's University. She has a special fondness for music and often plays Moonlight Sonata on the four-stringed lute.

(8) The two little girls, Wang Fu and Xu Congmei, look very similar and are just like twin students performing the Butterfly Dance, especially gracefully (Wang Rujia).
